# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Query Caching Layer Architecture

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement the query result cache: the cache key generation, the cache backend abstraction (in-memory vs Redis), the cache TTL policy, and the cache invalidation on dashboard save.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

81-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the research on the Grafana query result caching layer. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I've identified **9 core Go files** implementing the query result cache architecture in grafana/grafana:

### **Cache Key Generation** 
- `pkg/services/caching/service.go`: The `GetKey()` function generates cache keys using SHA256 hashing of JSON-serialized requests, prefixed with datasource UID

### **Cache Middleware**
- `pkg/services/pluginsintegration/clientmiddleware/caching_middleware.go`: Intercepts `QueryData()` and `CallResource()` requests, checks cache, executes queries on miss, and stores results

### **Cache Backend Abstraction**
- `pkg/infra/remotecache/remotecache.go`: Abstract `CacheStorage` interface with encryption and prefix wrappers
- `pkg/infra/remotecache/redis_storage.go`: Redis backend with TLS, authentication, connection pooling
- `pkg/infra/remotecache/memcached_storage.go`: Memcached backend 
- `pkg/infra/remotecache/database_storage.go`: SQL database backend with 10-minute garbage collection

### **Configuration & TTL**
- `pkg/setting/setting_remote_cache.go`: `RemoteCacheSettings` configures cache type, connection, encryption, and prefix
- Default TTL: 24 hours, configurable per datasource

### **Monitoring**
- `pkg/services/pluginsintegration/clientmiddleware/caching_metrics.go`: Prometheus metrics for cache hits/misses and request latency

### **Cache Invalidation Strategy**
- TTL-based expiration (default 24h)
- Explicit deletion for secrets/config changes
- Database backend automatic GC every 10 minutes

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details including file paths, symbol definitions, execution chains, and architectural narrative.

as a middleware-based system that intercepts query and resource requests at the plugin backend level. The architecture comprises several key components:\\n\\n### 1. Cache Middleware (`pkg/services/pluginsintegration/clientmiddleware/caching_middleware.go`)\\nThe `CachingMiddleware` class implements `backend.HandlerMiddleware` and intercepts both `QueryData()` and `CallResource()` requests. For each request:\\n- It calls `HandleQueryRequest()` to check if results are cached\\n- On cache hit, returns cached response immediately\\n- On cache miss, executes the actual query and calls `UpdateCacheFn()` to store results\\n- Integrates request deduplication to prevent duplicate concurrent requests\\n- Records cache performance metrics (hit/miss rates, request duration)\\n\\n### 2. Cache Key Generation (`pkg/services/caching/service.go`)\\nThe `GetKey()` function generates cache keys from query requests:\\n- Uses `JSONEncoder` to serialize the entire query request to JSON\\n- Applies SHA256 hashing via `SHA256KeyFunc()` to create a deterministic, fixed-length key\\n- Prefixes the key with the datasource UID to isolate caches per datasource\\n- Format: `{dataSourceUID}:{sha256_hash}`\\n\\n### 3. Cache Service Interface (`pkg/services/caching/service.go`)\\nThe `CachingService` interface defines two core methods:\\n- `HandleQueryRequest()`: Checks cache and returns `CachedQueryDataResponse` with optional update function\\n- `HandleResourceRequest()`: Similar pattern for HTTP resource requests\\n- The OSS implementation (`OSSCachingService`) is a no-op that always returns cache misses (caching is an enterprise feature)\\n\\n### 4. Cache Backend Abstraction (`pkg/infra/remotecache/remotecache.go`)\\nThe `RemoteCache` class provides unified access to different cache backends via the `CacheStorage` interface:\\n\\n**Supported Backends:**\\n- **Redis** (`pkg/infra/remotecache/redis_storage.go`): Uses go-redis client, supports TLS, password auth, connection pooling\\n- **Memcached** (`pkg/infra/remotecache/memcached_storage.go`): Uses gomemcache client\\n- **Database** (`pkg/infra/remotecache/database_storage.go`): Stores in `cache_data` SQL table with garbage collection every 10 minutes\\n\\nThe `RemoteCache` wrapper class applies optional decoration layers:\\n- **Encryption Wrapper** (`encryptedCacheStorage`): Encrypts cached values using the secrets service\\n- **Prefix Wrapper** (`prefixCacheStorage`): Adds a configured prefix to all cache keys for namespace isolation\\n\\n### 5. Cache Configuration (`pkg/setting/setting_remote_cache.go`)\\nThe `RemoteCacheSettings` struct configures cache behavior:\\n- `Name`: Cache type (\\\"redis\\\", \\\"memcached\\\", or \\\"database\\\")\\n- `ConnStr`: Connection string for Redis/Memcached\\n- `Prefix`: Optional key prefix for namespace isolation\\n- `Encryption`: Boolean flag to enable encryption of cached values\\n- Default TTL is 24 hours (configured in `defaultMaxCacheExpiration` in remotecache.go)\\n- Per-query TTL can be overridden via datasource configuration\\n\\n### 6. Cache Metrics (`pkg/services/pluginsintegration/clientmiddleware/caching_metrics.go`)\\nPrometheus histograms track cache performance:\\n- `grafana_caching_query_caching_request_duration_seconds`: Query cache request latency\\n- `grafana_caching_resource_caching_request_duration_seconds`: Resource cache request latency\\n- `grafana_caching_should_cache_query_request_duration_seconds`: Time spent evaluating whether to cache (AWS async queries)\\n\\n### 7. Request Deduplication Middleware\\nThe `requestDeduplicationMiddleware` prevents duplicate concurrent requests using Go's `singleflight.Group`:\\n- When N requests execute the same query simultaneously, only 1 query executes\\n- Other N-1 requests wait for the first result and use the same response\\n- Cache key is derived from datasource UID and query request\\n\\n### Cache Invalidation Strategy\\nThe cache relies on:\\n1. **TTL-based expiration**: Cache entries expire after their configured TTL (default 24h, configurable per datasource)\\n2. **Explicit deletion**: Individual cache entries can be deleted via `RemoteCache.Delete()` (used when secrets change, etc.)\\n3. **Database GC**: For database backend, expired entries are cleaned up every 10 minutes by `databaseCache.internalRunGC()`\\n\\nNote: Cache invalidation on dashboard save is not explicitly implemented via hooks. Instead, the caching operates at the query execution level - dashboard changes don't automatically invalidate; queries return cached results until expiration. This is the enterprise caching feature design.\\n\\n### Enterprise vs OSS\\n- **OSS**: `OSSCachingService` is always used, which returns cache misses (no-op)\\n- **Enterprise**: Enterprise caching service implementations would be provided that actually use the `RemoteCache` backend\\n\"\n}\n",
